Children's Special

Summer Vacation Special Page: A Few Things to Do During Summer Vacation 220

— Lan Shan

Little friends, summer vacation has already begun! Freed from the fixed school curriculum, you must feel a great sense of relief and be very happy to be able to enjoy the long two-month vacation!

But you must think about it: the vacation is two months long, and it would be very uneconomical to let it pass by completely blank – time is more valuable than money! I hope you will do the following things I suggest:

(1) Make Up for Failing Subjects

In school, aren't there one or two subjects that you find very difficult to understand? During the final exams, weren't there one or two subjects that you almost or actually failed? This is because you usually think they are difficult and have a fear of difficulty, and you haven't made a good effort to memorize them, so when the final exam comes, you panic and can't answer the questions. This is enough to drag down your other subjects and lower your average score. If there are too many failing subjects, it may even cause you to repeat the grade or be demoted! I advise you not to panic. You can use this vacation to make up for these subjects, and under the guidance of your parents, older siblings, diligently review them. No matter how difficult it is, you will eventually succeed.

(2) Read Some Beneficial Books

Those of you who have passed all subjects in the final exams, in addition to still needing to review your schoolwork, can read some valuable books, such as biographies of world celebrities, scientists, etc. As for other novels, fairy tales, and stories, it is best to ask your parents or older siblings to recommend them to you. Those books with gods and monsters and absurd plots are of no benefit to read, so it is better not to read them at all. You should read the newspaper every day.

(3) Practice Writing and Correspond with Friends

In school, there is a subject called composition. Sometimes the teacher gives the topic, and sometimes it is a free topic. These are all ways to improve your Chinese and make your thinking more flexible. During the vacation, you can continue to write compositions as usual, write some narrative essays, or write some argumentative essays. Show them to your parents and older siblings for feedback. If you like drawing, you can learn to draw more during the vacation. During the vacation, you are temporarily separated from your classmates, so you can use the method of correspondence to talk to them, which can also improve your Chinese.

I know you will definitely be able to do the above three things. But don't study too hard either. Playtime is also essential. I think the best time for reviewing and writing is from about six to nine o'clock in the morning. The weather is relatively cooler at this time, so you won't get too tired. After finishing your homework, you should rest and play. In your spare time, you should help your mother with some small tasks around the house because your mother is too tired.

Only in this way can we say that we have not wasted this long vacation!

The Fearsome Summer 221

— Wan Wen

The summer that people detest is becoming more severe day by day, hot and blazing, illuminating the entire earth, making energetic people weary, withering green and shady leaves, and causing beautiful and lovely flowers to droop. But despite your dislike, it still stands proudly there when its time comes.

Even wealthy people cannot withstand the threat of summer, so they stay at home, eating cold food, turning on electric fans, and enjoying themselves leisurely, except for those farmers who still work under the scorching sun, tanning their skin black and blistering it. But they have no choice but to do so for survival.

Even lively insects know the severity of the sunlight, and they all hide away. Only a few beautiful butterflies dance weakly in the flower bushes under the relatively weaker sunlight, and the cicadas on the willow trees chirp with shrill and pleasant cries.

Whether dense or sparse, the leaves droop or wither. In short, when the strong sunlight shines high, all phenomena of nature are withered and scorched.

The intense summer cannot last forever. When the goddess of the night is about to descend, its heat gradually weakens, and its brilliance slowly fades. At this time, everything in nature gradually becomes active again. People enjoy the cool under the bright stars and moon, engaging in lively discussions. Various insects display their skills, performing in this natural night, especially the good singers among them, as if opening a grand concert. Flowers, plants, and trees gradually return to their original state, preparing to soak up a refreshing dose of dew! But when the scorching sun returns tomorrow, people will still be weary, flowers and trees will still wither, and insects will still hide.

Summer Holiday Toys 222

— Zi Liang

Children! In addition to reading and studying, we should also use our own hands to create things! Not only is it very interesting, but it is also enough to discover our children's intelligence and wisdom. Like Watt, who studied science as a child and later invented many things. Children, let's invent something!

These days are hot days. Buy a large piece of ice from the ice seller and make various scientific toys!

(1) Prism: A prism is a triangular glass column. When sunlight passes through this triangular glass, it separates a beautiful band of seven-colored light. However, it is very expensive to buy a prism. Let's make one out of ice to play with. You can take thick ice and place it on a hot stove to make a long, regular triangle. Then take it to the sunlight, preferably sunlight entering the room. After the sunlight passes through the triangular ice prism, you can see a beautiful band of seven-colored light on the wall, as beautiful as the rainbow in the sky. If you get such a beautiful light band for a moment, don't rush. You only need to slightly rotate the triangular ice prism in your hand so that the sunlight passes through it and falls on the wall, revealing the seven-colored light band.

(2) Convex Lens: Take a piece of clean and thick (must be very transparent) ice and make it into a circular shape that is thick in the center and thin at the edges. You can carefully place it on a hot stove to make it. This work is a bit difficult, but if you do it carefully, you will definitely be able to make a good convex lens. After this convex lens is made, you can use it to play. First, you can use it as a magnifying glass to read books, and the small print in the books will be greatly enlarged. You can also use it to look at other small things. But it may be a bit blurry, of course, it is not as good as a convex lens made of glass.

Thirst 223

— Lu Guowei

Children, summer has arrived, and the weather is getting hotter day by day. Sweat is constantly dripping from your foreheads, and your mouths often feel very thirsty. Although you drink tea, your mouth becomes thirsty again after a while, unlike in winter, when drinking some tea is enough for the whole day. Isn't this very mysterious and strange? If children want to know this riddle, then let's all study the problem of thirst together.

(1) Why do we get thirsty? Our bodies contain a lot of water. This water is used to wash the various organs in our body. The washed water becomes sweat and urine, which are excreted from the body. At this time, because the body lacks water, it has to seek new water to replenish it. Therefore, we feel thirsty. However, why is it easier to get thirsty in summer? This is because the weather is hot in summer, and the body excretes a lot of sweat. The function of sweat is to reduce body temperature and resist external heat. Because we sweat a lot, we often feel thirsty.

(2) How should we quench our thirst? If we want to drink a lot of water for a long time without being thirsty, this is not right, because our body only needs to absorb a certain amount of water. The excess tea is of no use at all, and it only increases the amount of sweat. Therefore, tea should not be drunk too much or too quickly. It is best to drink it slowly and not too much. There is also a very good method of quenching thirst to introduce to children, which is to put tea in a small-mouthed bottle or a pointed-spout teapot. When drinking, let the tea flow into the throat like a line. This was invented by farmers working in the fields in southern Spain. In this way, a small amount of tea can be used to quench thirst. Isn't it convenient?

(3) When should we drink water and what kind of drinks should we drink? We should drink when we are thirsty, which goes without saying. And because of the different physical conditions and work of each person, we cannot specify how much time is appropriate to drink water. However, there is one thing to pay attention to: it is not advisable to drink too much after meals, as drinking too much will hinder digestion. As for the issue of beverages, the best beverage is of course boiled white water. It is not very harmful for adults to drink some tea and coffee. But children, I advise you to drink white water as the most suitable.

Summer 224

— Zhen

How to Make Sky-Blue Light Bulbs 225

— Bian Beichen

The bright and dazzling light of electric lights can greatly affect people's sleep and work in summer nights. Therefore, in summer, most people replace white light bulbs with sky-blue light bulbs because their color is soft, elegant, and blue, which is easy to induce sweet sleep and promote physical health.

If we go to an electrical appliance store to buy them, each one costs about three or four dimes. However, the sky-blue light bulbs sold in electrical appliance stores have a minimum brightness of 50 watts. If a family installs three 25-watt electric lights, and in summer they replace them with three 50-watt sky-blue light bulbs, assuming that each electric light is turned on for four hours every day, then the electricity bill will increase by more than one yuan per month!

Therefore, in order to reduce electricity bill expenses, we need to make our own sky-blue light bulbs with lower brightness.

The method of making sky-blue light bulbs is very simple. You only need to buy a bottle of "Celluloid Solution" from the pharmacy, and then buy a few copper-colored Prussian blue dyes from a paint store or cigarette paper store, pour them into the celluloid solution and stir. The depth of the color depends on your needs. Then take a light bulb with a wattage that suits you, dip it into the celluloid solution and Prussian blue that have been stirred evenly, and take it out. After it is air-dried, it can be used.

Children, why not give it a try!

Emphasize Cleanliness 227

— Twelve-year-old Liu Zhutong

Calligraphy and Painting on Banana Leaf Fans 228

— Chen Shicong

In this extremely hot summer, almost all children are holding a fan in their hands to fan themselves. Among them, I can say that a large part of them are using banana leaf fans because they are not only very cheap and durable, but also the wind is stronger than any other fan. However, it is very difficult to add calligraphy and painting to make it beautiful—because it is easy to fall off—but in fact, it is not. Now there is a very good and simple method to make it beautiful and easy to do. Children may wish to try it!

First, use a piece of straw paper to wipe the banana leaf fan all over! Otherwise, the words cannot be written on it—then you can use a pen to write and draw arbitrarily. After writing, light a wax candle—a kerosene lamp is also fine—and slowly smoke the side of the fan with the words and paintings on it, keeping it about an inch away from the flame. After smoking, wash it with clean water. Then, very beautiful black characters on a white background will appear. If you write a few poems or maxims on it, wouldn't it be elegant? If you write your own name well, you can prevent it from being lost.

Ten Commandments of Children's Hygiene in Summer 229

— Yao Mingran

(1) Do not eat excessively cold foods.

(2) Eat less candy, ice cream, soda water, watermelon, etc.

(3) Do not be greedy for coolness, so as not to get sick.

(4) Get up early and go to bed early, and practice deep breathing.

(5) Clothes must be clean, preferably white.

(6) Beware of epidemic colds and other diseases, and treat them quickly.

(7) Bathe every day. Do not take cold water baths in the river to avoid drowning and getting sick.

(8) Flies must be captured with a fly swatter and burned after capture.

(9) Before sleeping, drive away mosquitoes or light mosquito coils to drive them away.

(10) Operate less during the day and enjoy the cool in the evening.

Little Scientific Knowledge

Testing the Distance of Thunder 230

— Little Brother

Children, in the summer, I believe that none of you are not somewhat afraid of thunder. That's right, thunder is a scary thing. However, if we can know that the place where the thunder strikes is still very far from where we are, we don't have to be afraid at all. On the contrary, if it is very close, then we should find a way to hide. Therefore, the most important thing is to know the distance between the place where the thunder strikes and ourselves. The method of testing the distance is very simple: starting from seeing the lightning, immediately put three fingers of your left hand (index finger, middle finger, ring finger) on the root of your right thumb and measure the number of pulse beats until you hear the thunder. Then multiply the measured number of pulse beats by 340, and it can tell you how far the place where the thunder strikes is from you. For example, if you hear the thunder after your pulse beats five times after seeing the lightning, then the place where the thunder strikes is 5×340＝700. Two kilometers outside the meter. (It's still very far, so you don't have to be afraid at all.)

Children, don't you think this calculation method is very strange? In fact, there is nothing strange about it after an explanation. Because the speed of sound is 340 meters per second, and each pulse beat takes about one second. So, always using the above example to buy, the pulse beats five times, which means that the thunder took five seconds to reach your ears. According to the theorem in physics, the speed of sound is 340 meters per second, so the distance that the thunder traveled to your eardrum in five seconds is 5×340＝1700. In other words, the distance between the place where the thunder strikes and you is 1700 meters. This is the principle of the method of testing the distance of thunder.

Homemade Soda 231

— Feng Defu

The weather is getting hotter day by day, and all kinds of epidemic bacteria are gradually becoming active and starting their deadly work. Therefore, we must pay special attention to everything we eat and drink during this period and be especially clean.

Regarding drinking: Soda is indeed the most hygienic and beneficial to the body, so it is enjoyed by the general public, especially children, who like it very much. Then we should make it ourselves. It can be used as a game to pass the hot summer.

The following is a simple method for making soda:

Materials - 5 parts of sodium bicarbonate, 3 parts of citric acid, 12 taels of clear water. Utensils - one bottle (preferably a used soda bottle), one stopper. Method - First boil the clear water and let it cool completely, then pour it into a soda bottle that can hold twelve taels. Then weigh five parts of sodium bicarbonate, put it in the water bottle, hold the bottle mouth tightly with your palm, and shake it up and down to dissolve it. Then weigh three parts of lemon, add it to the bottle, and then quickly plug the bottle cap. The most important thing to pay attention to is not to let it vent. After this procedure is completed, immediately turn the soda bottle upside down. After a while, the homemade soda will be successful! If we want it to be sweet, we can add a few grains of sugar - ordinary sugar is also fine - if we also want it to be fragrant, we can also add some spices at will, such as banana oil, orange oil... sold on the market - just add a small drop. The last sentence is that before manufacturing, be sure to wash your hands and utensils clean to avoid any bacteria mixing into the soda and causing disease.

Children, if we can do it according to the above method, it will taste as beautiful and delicious as the soda bought on the market. Let's try it.

The King and the Shepherd Boy (2) 232

— Xin

In the year that the blond Hua Le was born, his father passed away. He ascended the throne and became king, which can be considered a small king who had never been seen before. He wore a crown on his head, which was heavy and made his head ache. His sad mother smiled and said that he must learn how to be a wise king. In this way, he had to learn thousands of lessons. Every time ten teachers wanted to put books and arithmetic into his head, he often looked out the window, watching the various changes in the weather. Oh, he was so eager to run outside the door and be in the wind, frost, rain, and snow!

One day, the dark-haired Hua Le was guarding his flock of sheep, sitting on the high hillside, playing the flute, accompanying his loneliness, when suddenly a very large fierce dog came. Hua Le's loyal sheepdog suddenly pricked up its ears and growled lowly in its throat. The fierce dog swept across the ground, and in that instant, the two dogs were wrestling together. Hua Le was startled and used his staff to forcefully separate them, but neither side was willing to give in. Fortunately, four knights whipped their horses and rushed up. It turned out that they were all the little king's guards.

One of the four, the tallest one, opened his mouth and said, "Child, we are here, you have to be careful. If your dog hurts the Lord's beloved dog, it will be bad for you."

The dark-haired Hua Le replied angrily, "It's your dog's fault! It attacked my dog first!"

The man scolded rudely, "Be quiet! The King is here. You impolite child, quickly bow deeply to the King!"

At this time, the blond Hua Le had already ridden his horse over. The dark-haired Hua Le had never seen such a beautiful picture. When he saw the magnificent little king, he was simply surprised and breathless. The little king was wearing a gorgeous blue velvet dress with silver trim, which shone brightly. On his golden-haired head, he wore a glittering golden crown.

The little king said softly, "I am very happy that your dog was not injured. How long have you raised it?"

Firefly Lamp 233

— Cheng Zhenru

Children, in this summer, there is a kind of lamp that does not cost money and will not burn your fingers. It is very fun to carry, and it is indeed a good toy for children to enjoy the cool in the night. Let me teach you how to make it.

(Materials) (1) One salted duck egg shell, do not cut it open with a knife. Take it and shine it in a bright place. Choose a hollow end, face it against the table, and gently tap it a few times. Then carefully pierce the shell at the broken head. After making a hole, use chopsticks to dig out the egg inside and eat it. Be careful when digging, and dig it clean without breaking the shell. (2) One cotton thread, one foot long is enough. (3) A small piece of white cellophane or white mulberry paper. (4) One-foot-long small bamboo stick. (Utensils) One small pair of scissors, a little paste. After you have prepared all the materials and utensils, you can start making it.

Use scissors to cut the broken head of the egg flat, and then cut the other head flat to form a drum shape (note that when cutting this head, first insert a small hole with the tip of the scissors, then it will be easier to cut), and then insert a small hole in the middle of the egg shell, like a pea, as shown in Figure (1). Then cut off a three-point length from the pointed end of the bamboo strip, tie it firmly with thread, as shown in Figure (2). Pass the thread through the hole in the mountain egg, and then paste the prepared paper on both ends of the egg shell, and then cut a small square of paper, as shown in Figure (3), and pass it through the thread to cover the small hole in the middle of the egg. Then tie the end of the thread to the bamboo stick, so the lamp is successful, as shown in Figure (4). It is best to draw some patterns or national emblems on the paper with colored pens, which will look even better. After the lamp is made, can't you burn candles inside? Without light, isn't it not fun? We made this lamp because we have something special that emits light. This thing was invented by Che Yin, a friend from the Jin Dynasty who studied hard despite his poverty. It is a firefly. You can find it at night in any wilderness where there is grass. We use a fan to catch a few and put them in the lamp, and it is a sparkling lamp, and it flickers, which is very artistic and very fun.

A firefly is a small insect. How can it emit light? Let me tell you, it has a light-emitting organ at its tail. When it breathes, air enters and produces an oxidation reaction, which emits light. It can also help us catch pests in the fields. It is a beneficial insect that greatly benefits our crops.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Amateur Weekly

The Confession of a Working Woman

Woman Reporter 234

— Miss Jiang Yixiao Discusses

Nestled serenely and comfortably at the foot of the winding and majestic Jiulong Mountain, by the clear and limpid Furong River, lies a tiny village named "Chenshu," which is my hometown.

I was born in a family within Wuxi, once quite wealthy but later declined and impoverished. My grandfather engaged in commerce after the Taiping Rebellion and accumulated some wealth, acquiring some land and property, making him a relatively prominent figure in the small village. However, my father was a scholar by training and also kind and gentle by nature. Consequently, after inheriting my grandfather's estate, he not only failed to maintain it but also suffered losses in every business venture. By the time I was twelve or thirteen, my family had reached a state of profound gloom and hardship, though outwardly, we tried desperately to maintain a façade of respectability.

With the help of some private savings of my mother's and the enthusiastic assistance of teachers and friends, I progressed from primary school to middle school, from middle school to university, eventually graduating. I wonder how I managed to survive over a decade of arduous and impoverished student life in this money-driven society? Looking back now, it feels somewhat bewildering! And somewhat astonishing!

Before I discuss my career path, I must first speak about the aspirations I held when I entered university. I was very young when I graduated from middle school, with no understanding of the world. My veins coursed with fervent passion, and my mind was filled with wonderful fantasies. Truly, it was an era of not knowing "how high the sky is or how thick the earth is." I always believed that anything I could imagine, I could achieve with courage and effort. In this state of mind, I entered the chemistry department of the science faculty at university. At that time, I held myself in high esteem, even believing, somewhat boastfully, that "in all the world, who but I is capable?" I looked down upon studying liberal arts, researching empty theories, and writing impractical essays, feeling that they could not save China from poverty and weakness. But studying chemistry? I would invent many daily necessities, start factories to manufacture them myself, not only profiting myself but also resisting foreign goods and saving a considerable amount of money flowing out of the country for the nation. After I became wealthy, I could establish many beneficial social enterprises, schools, hospitals, factories, charitable organizations… Such an ideal paradise was built in my then-ethereal and empty mind, making me always very happy and interested in diligently studying chemistry at university for four or five years.

However, after graduation? The elusive reality of society always presented various constraints, preventing me from realizing my ideals. No matter how much I wanted to have a "self-assertive" dream, that dream never came. The pressure of life pushed me into the teaching profession, wielding a writing brush and working as a scribe, and I mostly taught Chinese, with a small amount of mathematics. I spent about ten years in such monotonous seclusion, confined between my desk, chalk, and blackboard, nine years in Tianjin and one year in Beiping. At that time, an atmosphere of gloom enveloped North China, and the surging tide of the South had not yet gathered much momentum. Although I was quite dissatisfied with that rigid life, I could only wait for the right opportunity. Therefore, the Hebei Provincial Water Conservancy College and Hongde Middle School temporarily became my places of refuge. However, since I could not invest my hopes in a career, I could only express them in writing. Moreover, this was the motivation for my later career as a journalist.

My earliest writings, scattered pieces on women's issues, were quite numerous, mostly published in the Guowen Zhoubao (National News Weekly), with translations being the majority. This was around 1926. In 1927, I published a single-volume novel, "Lu Jian," which was written in epistolary style, focusing on psychological analysis. Although it was a novel about love, it also contained a noteworthy women's issue. At that time, Mr. He Xinleng, the editor of Guowen Zhoubao, often encouraged me to write, making me more interested in researching and expressing opinions on various social issues. So, around June or July of 1928, when the Northern Expedition succeeded, I officially became a journalist, working for the Tianjin Dagongbao (L’Impartial) as a reporter and editor of local news, and began writing articles on the living conditions of working women in Tianjin.

I am a person full of curiosity. Studying chemistry in school could still provide me with some fresh things to play with, but when I completely wasted my time in the teaching career, it made me feel very painful. Therefore, I suffered a lot mentally and physically. Although I once had a year of illness in Beiping, my body could never be as lively and healthy as when I was studying in school. Only when I started working at Dagongbao, due to the sudden change in life, my spirits were lifted. Just to talk about the investigation of the living conditions of working women in Tianjin, I worked hard for more than a year without slackening. Every day, I ran around on the streets, whether enjoying the warm spring breeze, or baking in the scorching sun and being soaked by the violent summer rain, or accompanied by the rustling leaves and stepping on the cold hail, I always spent my days with great interest all year round. I know myself that I have no constancy in everything, but engaging in this ever-changing life of a journalist is the only hobby I have gained. The only regrettable thing is that my body inevitably needs to be recuperated often! Last year, I followed my mother south from Tianjin and returned to my hometown to rest for a long time. This can also be considered a readjustment to my life.

I have a determination to do things, especially in the news industry, which I am very interested in! I think I am a person with a strong sense of self-confidence, and I like to understand the truth of everything directly and quickly. When I was working as a reporter, I could actually see the opposite lives of the lower-class laborers and the wealthy, and the detailed situation of the inner layer of society. Starting from curiosity, I can make myself not alienated from social life. At least, I can expose reality as much as possible in some opportunities for the reference of those who are responsible for reforming and promoting society.

Invisible chains are tightly binding the women of our country! What exactly is the crux of the women's issue that has been festering for thousands of years? Despite people advocating this movement and that movement, this deeply rooted chain still drags down those who sing high-sounding but impractical tunes. Therefore, in my personal experience, it is necessary to start with investigation and exposure, and only by knowing the root cause of the disease can we prescribe the right medicine. In order to do this willing work, I have not thought about organizing a family so far! Except for the sake of serving and raising a mother, I only promise myself to my reporting work.

In 1934, I published an autobiographical article in Guowen Zhoubao called "Childhood," which was a realistic report of my own family and individual. Recently, I am close to middle age, but I think that reporting the families and individual lives of all women in society is more universal and complete than simply writing about myself, isn't it? Moreover, for myself, it has indeed increased my infinite knowledge and experience in this work.

The "Interviews with Working Women" published in the local news section of Shanghai Dagongbao is continued and reported by me. Some people may think it is too trivial, but it may be welcomed by those who need to know in detail. I am not willing to presumptuously act as someone else's spokesperson, but I am willing to faithfully write out the inner groans of women in various industries!

The life of a reporter is not felt by those who are used to it, but if it suddenly comes, it will often make you at a loss! For example, if you set out to interview someone today, how will you start asking her? How can you grasp the center of her life to ask? How can you make her say as much as possible what she wants to say in a concise way?

Therefore, every time you decide to interview someone, you have to pay attention to some preparations that should be made. In experience, you have to simply record a few questions you want to summarize on paper in advance to avoid omissions. After meeting, if the other party is a person who likes to talk, you may wish to let her talk more. If it is a person who does not talk much, you have to find a way to induce her to talk! Otherwise, the talkative person will often be interrupted by you, and the person who does not like to talk will be silent relative to each other, wouldn't it be boring and tasteless to each other? And the result will be that you will not be able to grasp the key points and have no way to start reporting.

From 1928 to now, I have been engaged in the news industry for seven or eight years. In the daytime, I comb the wind and rain to hunt for information, and at night, I have to bury myself in the editing room to sort out manuscripts. I always have to go to bed at one or two o'clock. But because the complex inner layer of society has a variety of novel things, I will never feel tired and fatigued. When I was tired of living in Tianjin, Dagongbao happened to publish the Shanghai version again, which allowed me to change another environment. Although I only ran in Shanghai society for a few months, I think that the inner layer of Shanghai has at least several years for my research and exploration. In terms of my personality, maybe at that time, I will change another environment automatically.

Page 22

There are very few women in our news industry, and most of them are participating in the transaction and editing of a newspaper office, and it is really rare to be engaged in fieldwork. I have not met one in Tianjin or Shanghai!

In my continuous work, I understand that many women's issues are not simply one-sided, it is an important department of the entire social issue. We need the joint efforts of the whole society, especially the deep attention of colleagues in the industry and public opinion, and shout loudly. At the same time, the self-consciousness and efforts of our women's circles are of course extremely important.

"If you don't struggle, you can't survive!" I would like to bless the brave warriors of the women's world with this sentence! I hope we all have the determination to persevere to the end!

(Sincerely, Editorial Department of Shenbao Amateur Weekly).

Commentary

Building a New System of Remuneration 236

—

In the "Daily Talk" of the Education Daily on July 20th, Mr. Gong discussed "Building a New System of Remuneration." Besides criticizing the current teacher remuneration system for solely relying on empty qualifications ("academic credentials") as a standard, he also suggested a new system of remuneration. This issue has been discussed in the education sector for a long time, but I don't know why the education authorities "fear treatment and conceal their illness" regarding the current teacher remuneration standards.

I remember that during the May Fourth era, a man named Rao Shangda wrote an article called "Breaking Four Superstitions in the Intellectual World." He said that the biggest epidemic in the intellectual atmosphere at that time was: first, superstition of idols (because most people at that time were superstitious of celebrities); second, superstition of temples (because most people at that time were superstitious of the temples where celebrities were located, such as Columbia University, Peking University, Nanjing Higher Normal School, etc.); third, superstition of caves (because people at that time were also superstitious of the caves where the temples were located, such as Paris and London); fourth, superstition of spells (because as long as a person could say a few foreign words, he would be admired). More than twenty years have passed since the article was published, but looking at the situation of superstition of temples in the education sector today, it is still the same as it was twenty years ago, which is really frustrating.

The standards for hiring people and the standards for remuneration in all professions should be judged by the effectiveness of service, which is reasonable. However, relying solely on subjective examination often leads to arbitrary decisions. Although it may not differ too much in general, it is not a scientific method. Where does the so-called "effectiveness of service" differ? There are three necessary conditions:

First is learning. The level of knowledge and the length of ability of each person, in addition to innate wisdom, depends on whether the learning of each person is sufficient. Cultivating knowledge and skills comes from schools and later advanced studies. However, although schools are important places for cultivating knowledge and skills, it is not necessarily the case that entering a certain school can definitely obtain the knowledge and skills that are commensurate with that school. Because the efforts in school vary, just like the starting point of a race is the same, but the finish point will never be the same. Looking at the facts, those who have obtained graduation diplomas still have to go through various examinations, and the reason lies here. However, the learning we are talking about here does not only refer to the academic qualifications experienced in school, and later advanced studies account for the majority of each person's learning. From a practical point of view: the learning from advanced studies, such as the famous scholar Wang Yunwu, is more than twice as high as the students who have no learning and no skills but only have titles. Also, two people from the same school, one constantly studies after leaving school, and the other has neglected learning for a long time, try to think how much the learning of these two people should differ after ten years?

We do not deny that the "effectiveness of service" depends on the quality of each person's learning, but at the same time we also never admit that academic qualifications are the representative of learning, and diplomas can determine the effectiveness of service.

In today's society, especially in the education sector, the standards for determining the remuneration of service providers only see the brilliance of academic qualifications, but ignore the level of actual learning, so that those who are lucky to advance only know the importance of mixing qualifications, but do not know that hard work and advanced studies are more important. Who will be responsible for the formation of this trend, I ask the education administrative authorities?

The second is experience and ability. The size of service efficiency, experience and ability may be more important than learning. Many students who have only studied A+B or vertical line triangles often do not have the technical skills of apprentices. Similarly, for a teacher, how to set up school administration, how to make teaching materials suitable for children's needs, and how to adapt to children's personalities, such as these, a student who has just graduated from a normal school and an old teacher who has been in charge of teaching affairs for many years, due to their experience and experience, the impact on the teaching effect will also be very different. If we despise the valuable experience of old teachers and give them uniform treatment, or even old teachers have rich experience, but because of their academic qualifications—that is, the brand or title—being lower, even if they have excellent service effect, their treatment is still lower than those who have just emerged and have insufficient experience, how can we say that it is fair in terms of reason?

As for ability, its impact on the effectiveness of service is even greater. People who graduate from the same school and do the same job, but the abilities of the two are different. One can plan and control, making the affairs well-organized and achieving remarkable results. The other is weak in ability, has no specific plan before doing things, and has no unifying ability after doing things, and the result is naturally a mess. The so-called ability often comes from talent, which is not like learning that can be remedied by human efforts, but since we are talking about service efficiency, the level of ability of the service provider should naturally be one of the conditions for determining the remuneration standard.

The third is effort. For people who have all three conditions of learning, experience, and ability, if their efforts are insufficient, then the so-called service performance will still not be revealed. There is a story of the tortoise and the hare race that can provide a strong proof. We can say with certainty: those who only have sufficient learning and strong ability, but are not willing to continue with efforts, are the same as those who have no learning, no experience, and no ability. The service effect is still the same low or mediocre.

Overthrow "buying money with empty titles"! Oppose "worshiping temples"! People who do things should show their real skills! People who do things should enjoy the appropriate price for the efficiency they have achieved through their efforts! This is the slogan we have shouted for twenty years. I hope that from now on, all professional circles will set reasonable salary standards and correct the grievances of unequal treatment in the past.

Based on this, I agree with Mr. Gong's ninety suggestions for a new system of remuneration. In fact, starting with a uniform and equal minimum standard of salary for trial use has been seen in some institutions, but I don't know what reason there is for almost all places in the education sector to buy money with empty qualifications? If it is said that it is to improve the qualifications of teachers, then I think it is better to improve learning and reward experience, ability and effort.

Speaking of remuneration, it is not only about salary. All kinds of methods to seek happiness for service providers belong to the meaning of "remuneration". For example, the issue of opportunities for service providers to study and improve, the relationship between working hours and health, the issue of recuperation for illness and old age, the issue of maternity leave for female service providers, ... These are actually problems that we must solve when we directly seek happiness for service providers and indirectly seek progress in service efficiency. However, under the current unreasonable remuneration standard, these are even more felt that it is not worth talking about!

Industry Surveys

Refrigeration Industry in Shanghai 237

— Kuang Xinqin

There are two sentences in ancient Chinese books that say: "Families that store ice do not raise cattle and sheep." The meaning of this saying is very interesting! It implicitly praises the wonders of refrigeration. That is to say, families that can afford to store ice can simply place their slaughtered beef and mutton in the refrigerator to keep it fresh as usual, without having to raise livestock. In that pastoral era, because they didn't know how to make machine ice, they could only collect some natural ice blocks in winter to store. They also needed a suitable place, and only fairly wealthy families could afford such extravagance. But now in Shanghai, it is really very convenient. A dozen catties of machine ice only cost a dime or so (natural ice has gradually been eliminated). Why is it so cheap? This is because the refrigeration industry is developed. Moreover, Shanghai can boast that no matter what season it is, fresh vegetables and fruits can be bought all year round. And meat and fish are very difficult to spoil. As a joke, thanks to air-conditioning equipment and antiseptic injections, even the most perishable dead bodies can be kept in Shanghai for a month or two without changing!

Speaking of refrigeration, it makes one think of the "Crystal Palace" of the Dragon King in mythology. This kind of crystal palace-like place can already be seen in Shanghai during the ice factory period; but now, it has gone a step further and become 'you can't see the ice, but it's as cool as a "cold palace".' That is the effect of electric air-conditioning.

There are already many ice factories in Bailianjing and other places in Pudong, Shanghai. Last year, the reporter personally visited them. At that time, a friend from Pudong acted as a guide, and he prepared two wool robes in a suitcase to take with us. Outside the ice factory, the ninety-degree weather made us sweat profusely. As soon as we entered the factory gate, we saw towering ice mountains, and the cool air greeted us, scaring away the heat. When we walked into the middle, we felt like we were in the Guanghan Palace (the moon), and a burst of cold air was overwhelming. The friend had to take out the wool robes, and we quickly put them on, but we still felt unable to resist the cold. It is said that the workers working there all prepare very thick cotton-padded coats before they dare to stay for a long time, otherwise, they will at least suffer from severe typhoid fever.

This year can be regarded as Shanghai's air-conditioning year. Anyone in Shanghai who can get around has probably experienced the taste of air-conditioning, right? Cinemas, theaters, dance halls, grand hotels, and ice parlors all use air-conditioning to attract customers. More sophisticated office buildings and department stores also do so. But here we can only mention the "food aspect" and specifically introduce Shanghai's "refrigeration industry".

According to statistics, there are more than 20 refrigeration enterprises in Shanghai run by both Chinese and Westerners (including cold storage, ice factories, air-conditioning warehouses, companies selling refrigeration equipment, air conditioners, ice machines, etc.), such as Shanghai Air Conditioning Company, Shanghai Clean Storage Company, Dahua Machine Ice Factory, Shanghai Machine Ice Factory, Jardine Matheson Air Conditioning Warehouse, Hongchang Air Conditioning Company, Qiaomao Air Conditioning Company, Qiaolong Machine Ice Factory, Oriental Machine Ice Factory, Maochang Machine Ice Factory, Yongxing Cold Storage Company, Renji Ice Factory, Chengyuanji Ice Factory, Xinya Ice Making Company, China Ice Box Company, Arctic Company, Tiankaida, Schenk & Co., York Trading Company, Melchers & Co., Sulzer Brothers Machinery Company, Lida Company, Haijing Trading Company, etc.

Large-scale cold storage can store as much as ten tons of food such as fish, meat, melons, and fruits. Its interior must be divided into three parts: one is the cold storage, one is the ice-making area, and one is the air-conditioning machine installation area. Large-scale air-conditioning equipment all uses the "indirect air-conditioning method". Electricity is generated by a motor and connected to an air compressor. Usually, liquid ammonia is used as a medium and injected once from the liquid receiver. When the compressor starts to operate, the ammonia enters the expansion coil through the expansion valve, turning into gas, and then is sucked by the compressor and discharged into the condenser. It is cooled with prepared cold water to remove its heat and make it liquid again. After passing through the expansion valve, it evaporates again and becomes a gas, which is used to absorb external heat. This cycle continues, maintaining the minimum temperature of the main equipment's cooling tower, so that the indoor heat can be dissipated to the outside as much as possible. In the specially made air-conditioning box of this machine, there are also fans and cold water sprayed inside, so that cold air continuously comes out. If the equipment is complete, the cooled water can also be made into ice cubes, which can not only increase the effectiveness of the cold storage but also be supplied to the outside world for use. The construction of the cold storage must also be specially made. Usually, ventilation pipes are installed from the ceiling to distribute the cold air throughout the room. Furthermore, ice cubes that have been made but not transported are continuously piled up in all corners of the room. Foods, etc., are mostly placed on iron shelves, some like long bookshelves, some like white iron in ships. Air-conditioning warehouses are simpler because they store non-food items, mostly supplies such as carpets and furs. As for the walls of the cold storage, they are like a large ice box, with cork boards covered in asphalt on the outside, interspersed with roofing felt (those with flat beds are more elaborate, often nickel-plated, and some also have this felt laid inside the roof). The outside is then coated with several layers of airtight and waterproof mixture to make it tight.

Some simple equipment only has an ice-making area, and the made ice is pushed up to surround the refrigerated items. Some places still use natural ice (because it is not eaten, there is no danger), so the cost can be lower. Those who go to refrigerate food and supplies are mostly regular customers. Except for companies like Shanghai Clean Storage Company, which publish price lists in newspapers, the prices in other places are often negotiated face-to-face. Moreover, those large merchants who sell food, vegetables, and fruits are almost all the owners of the cold storage.

As for the restaurants and cold drink shops that can be seen everywhere, they also need to have refrigerators (such as ice boxes, ice cabinets, etc.). Larger and more modern ones use electric refrigerators (for example, the kitchen of the International Hotel uses nearly ten Arctic electric refrigerators). Electric refrigerators can not only refrigerate items but also make ice (they can automatically make ice once every forty-five minutes. Ordinary four-foot ones can make six pounds of ice each time) for use. Older ones use wooden ice boxes, or some even build a small cold storage room with a large amount of natural water.

However, the manager of refrigerated food and supplies is very important! Large-scale air-conditioning projects do have a significant effect on regulating air and dissipating heat, so refrigerated food can stay fresh. But if the management is not proper, it can also make the food taste bland. This is most easily felt with beef and fish because temperatures below zero are the same as temperatures above the boiling point. Freezing it too much is the same as overcooking it, it doesn't taste good. Therefore, the business strategy of restaurants in the hot summer often depends on proper refrigeration to attract customers.

Recently, many catering companies have sprung up in Shanghai. They declare that they can serve those who need all kinds of fresh meat, fish, vegetables, and fruits, and can provide ingredients for dishes, from a few cents to dozens of dollars, large and small, and can be delivered by car in the shortest time. Sophisticated catering companies have small and complete refrigeration equipment in their own prepared vehicles because their business can reach Pudong in the east, Minhang in the south, Baoshan in the north, and Zhenru in the west. Without this kind of mobile cold storage, the food would have spoiled long ago.

Currently, most middle-class and above families in Shanghai also pay much attention to refrigeration and have electric refrigerators, ice boxes, and other equipment. With such cooling, fortunate Shanghainese rarely eat spoiled food.

Biographies of Famous People

British Prime Minister Baldwin 238

— Mo

Among British politicians, the most famous is probably the current Prime Minister Baldwin. He is the most active and longest-running person on the British stage. He is the current leader of the Conservative Party and has served as Prime Minister—Premier—three times. If you ask a British person: Who is the most famous person in your country, they will surely say Prime Minister Baldwin.

Baldwin is a typical English gentleman. He knows what politeness is. He often shows a pleasant face, expressing a gentle and detached expression, but he is eloquent, quick-witted, and decisive. Therefore, he is most welcomed by the old British gentlemen and capitalists. And he himself is most able to understand the will of these people. He understands that he must speak on behalf of these people in order to come to power in the current situation in Britain.

Stanley Baldwin was born on August 3, 1867, in Bewdley, Worcestershire, England. He came from a wealthy family, so he was able to enter university and receive higher education, and had the knowledge and skills for general social and political activities.

After leaving school, Baldwin worked in the Baldwin company run by his father. But he was very interested in political activities. Thus, in 1908, he was elected as a member of the House of Commons in his hometown. In 1921, he was appointed President of the Board of Trade and became a member of the cabinet. At this time, he had already joined the Conservative Party, and all his efforts were, of course, based on the Conservative Party's position. In October 1922, he overturned the Lloyd George coalition cabinet with a speech. Then, the Conservative Party leader Bonar Law became Prime Minister, and Baldwin jumped to become Chancellor of the Exchequer. The following year, Law retired due to illness, and Baldwin was given the great task of organizing a cabinet and becoming Prime Minister. At this time, his international and even domestic reputation in Britain was not very great, so his appointment to form a cabinet caused quite a surprise. Some British people didn't even know what kind of person he was at all. It is said that at that time, Cambridge University, where he came from, held a parent-teacher conference, and Baldwin also went to participate. At the meeting, he met the scientist Thomson, who had been a classmate for many years. Thus, such an interesting question and answer occurred:

"Your face looks familiar, may I ask your name!" Thomson asked.

"I am Stanley Baldwin," Baldwin said.

"Ah! Yes, I remember! But, Prime Minister Baldwin, what are you doing right now?"

Baldwin couldn't help but smile and replied: "I am the Prime Minister!"

At this point, the scientist Thomson was shocked. He stared at the Prime Minister opposite him, as if he didn't quite believe his ears and eyes.

However, this first Baldwin Conservative Party cabinet collapsed in less than a year. Then, in January 1924, the first Labour Party cabinet in Britain was formed by MacDonald. But in the British general election in October of that year, the Conservative Party defeated the Labour Party again and won a majority of seats in the House of Commons. Thus, Baldwin was appointed to form a cabinet for the second time. At this time, the most important things he did were: first, to build the Singapore naval base to protect the rights of the British Empire in the East; second, to sever relations with the Soviet Union; and third, to sign the Locarno Treaty, attempting to gather European powers to deal with the Soviet Union. These things were, of course, applauded by the general gentlemen of Britain. Therefore, his cabinet gained temporary stability. However, two years later, unfortunately, Britain experienced an unprecedented coal miners' strike, which almost immediately collapsed the Conservative Party cabinet. At this time, Baldwin could only say "God, grant peace," and could be said to be at a loss. By 1929, the result of the general election was that the Conservative Party was defeated by the Labour Party, and Baldwin's second cabinet resigned en masse in June.

In 1931, the British gold standard collapsed, and MacDonald's Labour Party cabinet was on the verge of crisis, submitting its resignation to the British Emperor. At this time, the cunning Baldwin knew the seriousness of the situation and the difficulties of the cabinet, so he decided to help MacDonald and organized the so-called nationally united National Cabinet, with Baldwin as Lord President of the Council. However, this so-called nationally united National Cabinet was actually under the control of the Conservative Party Baldwin. MacDonald was just his puppet. Therefore, at that time, some people said that the National Cabinet was "a cabinet of two prime ministers".

Originally, after the general election in October 1931, the Conservative Party's power expanded, and Baldwin could have come out to form a cabinet, but he, who was experienced in the world, did not immediately come forward. He was determined to let MacDonald continue to do it. By 1935, when MacDonald had been played by him to the point of disrepute, he came out to accept the appointment to form a cabinet and served as Prime Minister. This was Baldwin's third time in power.

This cabinet with Baldwin as Prime Minister was nominally still called the National Cabinet, but in fact, it was entirely controlled by the Conservative Party. Initially, the cabinet lineup was: Simon as Prime Minister, Hoare as Foreign Secretary, and Eden as Minister without Portfolio. But when the Italo-Ethiopian War broke out, Hoare resigned as Foreign Secretary because he advocated being pro-Italian and did not advocate imposing sanctions on Italy, and Eden replaced him. After sanctions were imposed on Italy, because Britain disregarded Hitler's threatening actions against world peace, France could not actively deal with Italy, and Mussolini's aggressive actions in East Africa increased unabated, putting British prestige and the fate of the League of Nations to the most serious test. During this period, the Baldwin cabinet was shaken and almost collapsed. Later, Italy announced the annexation of Abyssinia, and the League of Nations sanctions lost their positive effect. Moreover, some British gentlemen fundamentally opposed the sanctions. Therefore, Baldwin again steered according to the wind, advocating the cancellation of sanctions, the withdrawal of the Mediterranean fleet, and the re-invitation of the pro-Italian Hoare to join the cabinet. Recently, he even canceled the mutual assistance pact on the Mediterranean coast to please Mussolini.

However, in this eventful time in the world, it is really difficult to say how long Baldwin's political life can last. Not to mention anything else, even his son Oliver has opposed his political tendencies, which shows to what extent his credibility in Britain has fallen.

Social Science Lecture

The Origin of the Family 239

— Guanglu

If the family system is only to indicate the successive blood relationship of a certain group of sexually reproductive individuals, then it can be traced back to a very ancient time. Because even in the most primitive human beings who only constitute wandering groups of twenty or thirty people, we can regard it as the most primitive produced by a certain lineage. It is very clear that intermarriage between different races was prohibited long after the formation of human beings. Not interacting with each other until death and even killing each other were very popular customs among ancient barbarian tribes. Therefore, it can be determined with certainty that the most primitive human beings in a certain group all came from their own lineage and were produced by the same bloodline. However, if family relations are not simply interpreted as blood relations, but as a form and system of individual sexual union between two sexes, and even as a system that constitutes a small individual organization based on sexual relations in a large society, then although the family system must include sexual relations, blood relations, and even be born from these relations itself to become part of its establishment reasons, it cannot simply be regarded as a natural blood relationship and completely confused with the latter.

Looking at the sexual life in the earliest stage of human beings, it was just naturally practicing promiscuity. All women were the wives of all men, and all men were the husbands of all women. Not only were brothers and sisters all husband and wife to each other, but it was also common among parents and children. We can not only get proof from the ancient custom of only knowing the mother but not knowing the father, recognizing that at that time, the mother often had sexual relations with all men, so it was impossible to identify whose son it was. Only the mother who gave birth to and raised him could know. Moreover, McLennan cited the Koryaks of the Bering Strait, the Katak people of Alaska, and the Tinneh people of inland North America as evidence. Letourneau also cited the Cucos of Chile, the Carapies of Indochina, and the Kaso people as evidence. Since in the primitive social forms of human beings, sexual life was unregulated and unrestricted, then in sexual relations, it was only based on natural needs, and there was no customary regulation as a rule. It could not be called any artificial system. Therefore, the family system established based on sexual restrictions and its individual narrow blood system generally did not exist. If we want to call the sexual relations at that time a system, then at most it can only be called promiscuity. This system at most only existed naturally due to the requirements of natural instinct and did not contain the meaning of artificial regulations at all.

On the other hand, the social and economic life of primitive human beings was completely a shared way of life. At most, they could only reserve certain habitually used tools for production for personal use. Even these things still belonged to the group after death. Because of this, production labor was shared, and the harvest of production was also distributed jointly to all members. Individuals or smaller single groups in the common group could not be differentiated from the larger society, because there was no phenomenon of him or them individually owning any wealth. As a result of this shared social and economic system, that according to the combination of two affections and constituting a small special group according to its bloodline, and independently operating its economic life in a large society, that is, only providing labor to its own small group, and this small group privately owning its labor tools and all harvests, was fundamentally impossible. Therefore, this kind of small group that could independently manage all its own life did not exist and could not exist. That is to say, in the primitive common society, in economic relations, such an independent small individual private unit was not allowed to exist. The family in that sense cannot be said to have appeared in the primitive common society.

From the above reasons, the so-called family system, that is, if based on the independent organization of the small system of sex and bloodline, the organization of private life based on the small independent unit of economy, the general family system could not exist very early. Because at that time, sexual relations were not fixed, and even when children became adults, they were members of the common group, not members of a single family. In economic terms, because it was common, there was no possibility of differentiating from the public economic life and forming a separate economic system. Because of this, the so-called family system, in primitive society, even if we want to say that it has its roots, at most we can only say that the fundamental factors of sexual union and bloodline union on which it is based existed in the society at that time. However, the family system is dynamic, and its changes also change with the changes in social and economic relations. Therefore, if we scrape off the genes of its economic relations and only talk about the origin of the family system from the relationship of sex and blood, then we will not be able to explain anything.

However, there are many scholars who simply explain the origin of the family based on sexual union, believing that absolutely unregulated sexual intercourse never existed in human history. Human beings have always only had polygamy or polyandry, and monogamy is the supreme morality. Therefore, they argue that due to fixed sexual union, the family was already an existing form of human life, and the family system naturally existed from the emergence of human beings. Not only that, but they also seek basis in animals, believing that many birds are loyal to monogamy, and there is also monogamy or polygamy in primates and great apes. Even that kind of absolutely unregulated sexual intercourse among animals belongs to a lower stage. Therefore, it seems that the elements of this family system were established earlier in animals by the restriction of sexual union. Naturally, there is indeed monogamy among birds, but this is simply due to the physiological relationship that the group cannot help during the incubation period. In primates and great apes, not only has that kind of monogamy or polygamy not been proven without contradiction, but also primate apes are animals whose group life is relatively developed. Protecting young apes is no longer just the responsibility of their parents, but the responsibility of their group.

Home
